Good question.
This is not a cosmetic feature. This is core enterprise capability.

You’re describing:

UI drill-down navigation

Excel cross-sheet traceability

Parent → child → source trace chains

That is audit-grade explainability, not “nice-to-have UX”.

Let’s think structurally.

Where This Belongs in the Roadmap
You are currently at:

✅ Phase 1A – Governance & Control

✅ Phase 1B – FX Engine

🔄 Phase 1C – Consolidation + IC + Export

Drill-down and cross-linked exports belong inside Phase 1C, not later.

Why?

Because consolidation without drill-down is not CFO-grade.
A finance head will always ask:

“Show me where this number came from.”

If you delay drill-down:

You’ll design consolidation tables without trace IDs

You’ll miss linkable foreign keys

Excel exporter won’t embed row references

Retrofitting later will be painful

So the answer is:

👉 Design now. Implement inside Phase 1C.

Two Layers of Drilldown
You must implement drillability at two levels:

1️⃣ Runtime API Drilldown (UI Layer)
Every displayed object must be traceable backward.

Example hierarchy:

Consolidated Total
    ↓
Entity Contribution
    ↓
Line Item
    ↓
Source Snapshot Line
    ↓
Original artifact reference
This means:

consolidation_results must reference run_id

consolidation_line_items must reference snapshot_line_id

intercompany_pairs must reference consolidation_line_items

elimination records must reference intercompany_pairs

Drilldown endpoints needed:

GET /consolidation/run/{id}/account/{account_code}
GET /consolidation/run/{id}/entity/{entity_id}
GET /consolidation/run/{id}/line/{line_id}
GET /consolidation/run/{id}/snapshot/{snapshot_id}
No aggregated number should exist without a lineage path.

2️⃣ Excel Cross-Sheet Linking
This is where most systems fail.

If you export:

Sheet 1 – Consolidated P&L
Sheet 2 – Entity Breakdown
Sheet 3 – IC Eliminations
Sheet 4 – Unexplained
Sheet 5 – Source Lines

Then:

Each consolidated line cell must hyperlink to entity breakdown

Entity breakdown rows hyperlink to line items

Line items hyperlink to snapshot rows

IC sheet hyperlinks back to source line pairs

Excel supports:

HYPERLINK formula

Named ranges

Internal sheet anchors

Structured table references

You must:

Create deterministic row anchors

Generate stable named references

Avoid random ordering

This is not formatting — it is architecture.

When To Implement?
NOT Phase 1D
NOT “future enhancement”
NOT UI layer only
It must be:

🔒 Phase 1C – Built into the exporter and schema design

Because once persistence model is locked, retrofitting lineage fields becomes expensive.

What Must Be Added to Phase 1C Prompt
You should add one more requirement to the Codex implementation prompt:

All displayed numerical outputs must be drillable via deterministic lineage.

Consolidation export must implement cross-sheet hyperlink references:

- Consolidated totals link to entity breakdown rows
- Entity breakdown rows link to consolidation_line_items
- Line items link to normalized snapshot lines
- IC elimination rows link back to matched source rows

No aggregate number may exist without a lineage path.
Excel exporter must generate deterministic internal hyperlinks using stable row anchors.
Strategic View
If your vision is AI CFO Brain:

Drilldown + lineage = Explainable Finance Engine

That is what differentiates you from:

BI dashboards

Spreadsheet tools

Generic consolidation software

Without drilldown:
You are a calculator.

With drilldown:
You are an audit-ready intelligence system.

Good. Let Phase 1C implementation finish first.
Then we layer drillability properly — not as a patch.

Now to your deeper question:

Should any item in the platform be drillable to base snapshot / source lines / base input?

Short answer:

Yes — but in a structured way, not blindly everywhere.

Let’s think like a CFO building a $1B platform, not like a dashboard builder.

The Principle: Deterministic Financial Lineage
Every financial number must satisfy:

A displayed number must be traceable backward to its authoritative input artifact.

That means:

Display Layer
    ↓
Service Output
    ↓
Persisted Financial Record
    ↓
Normalized Snapshot
    ↓
Original Source Artifact
If you cannot traverse that path — it is not enterprise-grade.

Where Drillability MUST Exist
These are non-negotiable:

1️⃣ Consolidation totals
Must drill → entity contribution → line items → snapshot lines

2️⃣ IC elimination results
Must drill → pair → source lines → snapshot lines

3️⃣ FX variance outputs
Must drill → conversion record → effective rate → snapshot line

4️⃣ Month-end FX locked rate usage
Must drill → manual monthly rate entry → audit trail

5️⃣ Any exported Excel
Must contain internal hyperlinks that mirror API drill paths

Where Drillability is NOT Required
You don’t need drilldown for:

Configuration settings

Health checks

Cache statistics

Workflow logs

Derived metadata not representing financial impact

Drillability is required for:

Anything that affects financial numbers.

Architectural Rule Going Forward
You should adopt this permanent platform invariant:

No financial output may exist without a lineage path to a base snapshot line.

This becomes a design rule.

What This Means Structurally
You must ensure:

1️⃣ All consolidation tables carry foreign lineage
For example:

consolidation_line_items → snapshot_line_id

intercompany_pairs → consolidation_line_item_id (from + to)

consolidation_eliminations → intercompany_pair_id

consolidation_results → aggregation of line_items

No aggregation without reversible grouping key.

2️⃣ No “computed-only” numbers
If something is calculated and shown:

Either persist its derivation reference

Or compute it dynamically with drill parameters

Never show “floating math” with no lineage.

3️⃣ FX must never break lineage
Important:

FX conversion must not erase original local amount.

You must always preserve:

local_amount

fx_rate_used

expected_rate

parent_amount

fx_delta_component

That way:

parent_amount
    ↓
local_amount * fx_rate_used
    ↓
snapshot_line_id
Clean trace.

Should EVERYTHING in the platform be drillable?
Let’s be precise.

Not everything.

But everything in these domains:

MIS

Consolidation

FX impact

Variance

IC elimination

Revenue recognition

Prepaid amortization

Lease schedules

FAR

Yes.

Because those are accounting-impacting modules.

When Do We Implement Global Drilldown?
Phase-wise answer:

Phase 1C: Implement drillability inside consolidation + Excel exporter

Phase 1D+: Introduce a generic “Lineage Resolver Service”

That future service would:

GET /lineage/{record_type}/{id}
And recursively return full ancestry chain.

That is Phase 2 architecture.

Strategic Warning
If you try to implement global drilldown retroactively later:

You will have:

Missing foreign keys

2. Architectural decisions implemented

consolidation_runs is immutable run header; lifecycle status is append-only in consolidation_run_events with derived latest status via highest event_seq.
Implemented normalized snapshot abstraction (normalized_financial_snapshots, normalized_financial_snapshot_lines) and explicit entity-to-snapshot mapping in run requests.
Deterministic IC hierarchy only:
Tier 1: ic_reference + ordered entity pair + account_code
Tier 2: counterparty_entity + ordered entity pair + mirrored ic_account_class
Classification order implemented exactly: matched -> fx_explained -> timing_difference -> unexplained.
Explicit append-only elimination audit trail in consolidation_eliminations; no silent elimination.
Temporal payloads are compact (run_id, tenant_id, correlation_id, lightweight metadata); heavy data read/written in DB-backed activities.
Write paths use AuditWriter; new tables are RLS-enabled/forced and append-only trigger-protected in migration.
Correlation ID is propagated through API -> service writes -> workflow/activity payloads/events.
Fixed migration-history safety: 0003_phase1a now uses a frozen Phase-1A table list (prevents future table additions from breaking historical migration replay).

Create endpoints in:

New endpoints:

GET /api/v1/consolidation/run/{run_id}/accounts/{account_code}
GET /api/v1/consolidation/run/{run_id}/entities/{entity_id}
GET /api/v1/consolidation/run/{run_id}/line-items/{line_item_id}
GET /api/v1/consolidation/run/{run_id}/snapshot-lines/{snapshot_line_id}

Rules:

- Must validate run ownership
- Must return deterministic ordering
- Must return lineage metadata in response:
    parent_reference_id
    source_reference_id
    correlation_id

Each response must allow client to navigate to next level without recomputation.

No aggregation-only responses allowed.
Every drill response must include child references.

=======================================================

=======================================================

Create new module:

backend/financeops/services/consolidation/lineage_resolver.py

Responsibilities:

resolve_lineage(record_type: str, record_id: UUID)

Supported types:
- consolidation_result
- consolidation_line_item
- intercompany_pair
- elimination
- snapshot_line

Resolver must:

- Return full ancestry chain
- Include foreign key path
- Preserve correlation_id
- Be pure-read only
- Use RLS context

Do NOT introduce circular imports.
Do NOT embed business logic.
Resolver must be lightweight and modular.

=======================================================

backend/financeops/services/consolidation/excel_exporter.py

- Stable row anchors
- Use internal Excel HYPERLINK formula
- Links must navigate:
    Consolidated → Entity
    Entity → Line Items
    Line Items → Snapshot
    IC → Line Items
    Eliminations → IC pair

No business logic inside exporter.
Exporter consumes precomputed structured DTOs.

Hyperlink structure must not break deterministic checksum.
Use fixed sheet names.

- Verify every intercompany_pair references line_items

- Write failed event

- Abort finalize

Modular directory structure
backend/financeops/db/models/revenue.py, lease.py, prepaid.py, fixed_assets.py

backend/financeops/services/lease/ with lease_registry.py, payment_schedule.py, pv_calculator.py, liability_schedule.py, rou_schedule.py, interest_engine.py, remeasurement.py, lineage_validation.py, drilldown_service.py, service_facade.py
backend/financeops/services/prepaid/ with prepaid_registry.py, pattern_resolver.py, schedule_generator.py, journal_builder.py, adjustments.py, lineage_validation.py, drilldown_service.py, service_facade.py
backend/financeops/services/fixed_assets/ with asset_registry.py, depreciation_engine.py, life_policy.py, impairment_engine.py, disposal_engine.py, journal_builder.py, lineage_validation.py, drilldown_service.py, service_facade.py

backend/financeops/api/v1/revenue.py, lease.py, prepaid.py, fixed_assets.py, and router inclusion in api/v1/router.py
backend/financeops/temporal/revenue_workflows.py, revenue_activities.py, lease_workflows.py, lease_activities.py, prepaid_workflows.py, prepaid_activities.py, fixed_assets_workflows.py, fixed_assets_activities.py, plus worker registration
Tests mirrored by module under backend/tests/unit/ and backend/tests/integration/, with drillability + RLS + append-only coverage per engine
Data model definitions
Common control pattern per engine: <engine>_runs (immutable header) + <engine>_run_events (append-only lifecycle, derived latest status by max event_seq)
Common required columns on all financial-impacting tables: tenant_id, chain_hash, previous_hash, created_at, correlation_id, immediate lineage hook (source_*_reference), supersedes_id where versioning applies
Revenue tables: revenue_contracts, revenue_performance_obligations, revenue_contract_line_items, revenue_schedules, revenue_journal_entries, revenue_adjustments
Lease tables: leases, lease_payments, lease_liability_schedule, lease_rou_schedule, lease_modifications, lease_journal_entries
Prepaid tables: prepaids, prepaid_amortization_schedule, prepaid_journal_entries, prepaid_adjustments
FAR tables: assets, asset_depreciation_schedule, asset_impairments, asset_disposals, asset_journal_entries
Material tables are FinancialBase + RLS enabled/forced + tenant policy + append-only trigger
Key uniqueness examples: run signature uniqueness per tenant, schedule natural key uniqueness (run_id + source_line_id + period), idempotent event uniqueness (run_id + event_type + idempotency_key)
Lineage design per module
Revenue chain: recognized revenue row -> revenue schedule line -> performance obligation -> contract line item -> contract (source_contract_reference)
Lease chain: lease expense row -> liability/ROU schedule line -> lease payment -> lease (source_lease_reference)
Prepaid chain: amortized expense row -> amortization schedule line -> prepaid -> source expense snapshot (source_expense_snapshot_reference)
FAR chain: depreciation/impairment/disposal row -> depreciation schedule line -> asset -> acquisition snapshot (source_acquisition_snapshot_reference)
Every drillable row stores parent_reference_id, source_reference_id, correlation_id
Terminal event gate per run validates lineage completeness before completed/completed_with_warnings; on failure append failed event with structured missing-link metadata
Drilldown endpoint design
Revenue endpoints: POST /api/v1/revenue/run, GET /run/{id}, GET /results/{id}, GET /run/{id}/contracts/{contract_id}, GET /run/{id}/obligations/{obligation_id}, GET /run/{id}/schedule-lines/{line_id}, GET /run/{id}/journal-entries/{entry_id}
Lease endpoints: POST /api/v1/lease/run, GET /run/{id}, GET /results/{id}, GET /run/{id}/leases/{lease_id}, GET /run/{id}/payments/{payment_id}, GET /run/{id}/liability-lines/{line_id}, GET /run/{id}/rou-lines/{line_id}
Prepaid endpoints: POST /api/v1/prepaid/run, GET /run/{id}, GET /results/{id}, GET /run/{id}/prepaids/{prepaid_id}, GET /run/{id}/amortization-lines/{line_id}, GET /run/{id}/journal-entries/{entry_id}
FAR endpoints: POST /api/v1/far/run, GET /run/{id}, GET /results/{id}, GET /run/{id}/assets/{asset_id}, GET /run/{id}/depreciation-lines/{line_id}, GET /run/{id}/impairments/{impairment_id}, GET /run/{id}/disposals/{disposal_id}
Response contract mirrors 1C drillability: deterministic ordering, child reference IDs, lineage metadata, no recomputation-only responses
Read paths are pure-read and tenant-scoped async session with runtime RLS context active
Temporal workflow breakdown
RevenueRecognitionWorkflow: mark running -> load contracts/obligations -> allocate -> generate schedule -> build journal preview -> validate lineage -> finalize
LeaseAccountingWorkflow: mark running -> build payment timeline -> PV/liability/ROU schedules -> interest + amortization -> journal preview -> validate lineage -> finalize
PrepaidAmortizationWorkflow: mark running -> load prepaids -> resolve amortization pattern -> generate schedule -> journal preview -> validate lineage -> finalize
FixedAssetWorkflow: mark running -> load assets -> depreciation schedule -> impairment/disposal pass -> journal preview -> validate lineage -> finalize
Remeasurement workflows per module run as separate workflow types with same run/event controls
Workflow payload remains compact: run_id, tenant_id, correlation_id, requested_by, config_hash; heavy arrays stay in DB
Retry policy same style as 1C: bounded retries, non-retryable validation errors, idempotent activity writes
Idempotency model
Start requests build deterministic request_signature from normalized config + source references + tolerances/policy IDs
Duplicate request returns existing run_id/workflow_id instead of new run
Lifecycle events are append-only and idempotent via (run_id, event_type, idempotency_key)
Each activity first checks materialization existence via natural key constraints; retries become no-op reads
Corrections/remeasurements always new rows with supersedes_id; no in-place mutation paths
Journal preview runs use deterministic batch keys to avoid duplicate preview lines on retries
Remeasurement strategy
Revenue: contract modification appends revenue_adjustments; regenerate forward schedule version; cumulative catch-up line at effective date
Lease: modification appends lease_modifications; recalculate remaining liability at modification date with persisted discount-rate basis; delta adjusts ROU or P&L per policy code
Prepaid: adjustments append in prepaid_adjustments; superseding schedule lines from effective date forward
FAR: useful-life/residual/impairment/disposal events append; depreciation schedule re-baselined prospectively with explicit supersession linkage
Each remeasurement run has its own terminal lineage validation and immutable event trail
FX interaction strategy
Only call Phase 1B selected-rate surface (resolve_selected_rate, convert_daily_lines, apply_month_end_rate where applicable)
Revenue: usage/milestone/date-bound recognition uses daily selected rate; period-close recognition uses month-end locked mode
Lease: payment-date cash movements can use daily selected rate; period-end liability revaluation uses month-end selected rate; rate date persisted per schedule line
Prepaid: default month-end selected rate for period amortization; optional daily only when policy explicitly references transaction-date basis
FAR: depreciation generally uses policy-selected reporting basis; FX remeasurement is deterministic and policy-coded, never raw-provider-driven
Reuse FX cache behavior from 1B; no direct reads from fx_rate_quotes in accounting engines
Risk areas
Policy complexity drift across GAAP/Ind-AS variants can create branching explosion without strict policy versioning
Rounding drift across long schedules if quantization boundaries are inconsistent by stage
Missing locked FX rate for month-end runs can block deterministic close
Large tenant batches can stress workflow timeouts without chunking and pagination
Late or superseded source artifacts can trigger lineage invalidation if run snapshot contract is not frozen
Drillability payload size can grow quickly unless child references are paginated deterministically
Cross-module journal overlap risk requires deterministic journal reference namespace per engine
Suggested implementation sequence (1D.1, 1D.2, …)
1D.1 Platform scaffolding: add run/event framework reuse, lineage metadata contract, drill response base schema, worker registration skeletons.
1D.2 Revenue core: contracts/obligations/allocation/schedule/journal preview + drill endpoints + lineage gate.
1D.3 Lease core: lease registry, PV/liability/ROU/interest schedules + journal preview + drill endpoints + lineage gate.
1D.4 Prepaid core: prepaid registry + deterministic pattern engine + amortization/journal + drill endpoints + lineage gate.
1D.5 FAR core: asset registry + depreciation + impairment/disposal + journal preview + drill endpoints + lineage gate.
1D.6 Remeasurement pass: module-specific remeasurement workflows and supersession chains.
1D.7 Excel drill exports: per-engine multi-sheet exports with deterministic cross-sheet links and checksums.
1D.8 Hardening and full-suite: RLS runtime tests, append-only rejection tests, AuditWriter path assertions, Temporal retry/idempotency tests, cross-module deterministic pipeline run.

=======================================================
REVENUE LOGIC RULES
=======================================================

A. CONTRACT REGISTRY
- deterministic contract storage only
- no AI extraction
- no fuzzy parsing
- corrections via append-only superseding rows

B. PERFORMANCE OBLIGATIONS
- obligation records tied to contract
- SSP-based allocation support
- deterministic allocation only

C. ALLOCATION ENGINE
Implement deterministic allocation:
- contract consideration allocated based on standalone selling prices
- allocation total must reconcile exactly to total contract value
- quantization policy from accounting_common must apply
- rounding residual handling must be deterministic and test-covered

D. RECOGNITION METHODS
Implement core logic:

1. Percentage of completion
- deterministic input basis only
- use provided completion percentage or deterministic cost/effort ratio input
- no inferred percentages

2. Completed service method
- full recognition only when completion flag/event provided

3. Milestone-based
- recognize only on milestone trigger event/reference

4. Straight-line
- even allocation over defined recognition period

5. Usage-based
- recognize based only on provided deterministic usage quantity/input

E. REMEASUREMENT / MODIFICATION
Implement basic contract modification handling:
- append revenue_adjustments
- regenerate forward-looking schedule version
- create cumulative catch-up where policy requires
- no in-place mutation of previous schedule
- supersession linkage mandatory

F. FX INTEGRATION
- contract currency may differ from reporting currency
- use only Phase 1B selected-rate surfaces
- date-bound recognition can use selected daily rate when configured by policy
- period-close recognition can use month-end locked selected rate
- persist fx_rate_used per schedule line
- never read raw provider quote tables

G. JOURNAL PREVIEW
- deterministic preview only, not posting
- use journal namespace helper with REV- prefix
- one revenue journal line must trace back to schedule line
- journal rows must be drillable

=======================================================
LINEAGE + DRILLABILITY
=======================================================

Revenue drill path must support:

recognized revenue
→ revenue_schedules
→ revenue_performance_obligations
→ revenue_contract_line_items
→ revenue_contracts

Implement deterministic drill endpoints:

POST /api/v1/revenue/run
GET /api/v1/revenue/run/{run_id}
GET /api/v1/revenue/results/{run_id}
GET /api/v1/revenue/run/{run_id}/contracts/{contract_id}
GET /api/v1/revenue/run/{run_id}/obligations/{obligation_id}
GET /api/v1/revenue/run/{run_id}/schedule-lines/{schedule_id}
GET /api/v1/revenue/run/{run_id}/journal-entries/{journal_id}

Rules:
- use DrillResponseBase-compatible response shape
- include parent_reference_id
- include source_reference_id
- include correlation_id
- include child_ids
- pure read paths only
- deterministic ordering only

Lineage completeness gate:
Before terminal completed event:
- every schedule line must resolve to contract line item
- every contract line item must resolve to obligation or contract
- every journal entry must resolve to schedule line
If incomplete:
- append failed event
- error_code = LINEAGE_INCOMPLETE

- idempotent activity writes via natural keys and event idempotency

=======================================================
LEASE LOGIC RULES
=======================================================

A. LEASE REGISTRY
- deterministic lease storage only
- no AI extraction
- no fuzzy parsing
- corrections via append-only superseding rows

B. PAYMENT SCHEDULE
- deterministic generation from explicit lease inputs
- no inferred payments
- payment ordering by payment_sequence and payment_date

C. PRESENT VALUE CALCULATION
- deterministic PV calculation from:
  payment schedule
  persisted discount rate
- discount rate persistence required
- no black-box estimation
- test exact reproducibility

D. LIABILITY SCHEDULE
Implement deterministic schedule:
- opening liability
- interest accretion
- payment reduction
- closing liability

E. ROU SCHEDULE
Implement deterministic schedule:
- opening ROU asset
- amortization / lease expense
- impairment adjustment if present
- closing ROU balance

F. INTEREST ENGINE
- deterministic interest computation only
- no mixed lease/revenue/prepaid math
- quantization from accounting_common applies

G. REMEASUREMENT / MODIFICATION
Implement basic modification handling:
- append lease_modifications
- recalculate remaining liability from effective date
- use persisted discount-rate basis and modification policy
- create forward-looking superseding schedule version
- no in-place mutation of prior schedule

H. FX INTEGRATION
- if lease currency != reporting currency:
  - payment-date cash movement may use selected daily rate when policy says so
  - period-end liability remeasurement uses month-end selected rate
- persist fx_rate_used on schedule lines
- never read raw provider quote tables
- same-currency lease/reporting path must use 1.0

I. JOURNAL PREVIEW
- deterministic preview only, not posting
- use journal namespace helper with LSE- prefix
- one journal line must trace back to liability or ROU schedule line
- journal rows must be drillable

=======================================================
LINEAGE + DRILLABILITY
=======================================================

Lease drill path must support:

lease expense / liability movement
→ lease_liability_schedule or lease_rou_schedule
→ lease_payments (where applicable)
→ lease contract

Implement deterministic drill endpoints:

POST /api/v1/lease/run
GET /api/v1/lease/run/{run_id}
GET /api/v1/lease/results/{run_id}
GET /api/v1/lease/run/{run_id}/leases/{lease_id}
GET /api/v1/lease/run/{run_id}/payments/{payment_id}
GET /api/v1/lease/run/{run_id}/liability-lines/{line_id}
GET /api/v1/lease/run/{run_id}/rou-lines/{line_id}
GET /api/v1/lease/run/{run_id}/journal-entries/{journal_id}

Rules:
- use DrillResponseBase-compatible response shape
- include parent_reference_id
- include source_reference_id
- include correlation_id
- include child_ids
- pure read paths only
- deterministic ordering only

Lineage completeness gate:
Before terminal completed event:
- every liability schedule line must resolve to lease and, where relevant, payment line
- every ROU schedule line must resolve to lease
- every journal entry must resolve to liability or ROU schedule line
If incomplete:
- append failed event
- error_code = LINEAGE_INCOMPLETE

=======================================================
TEMPORAL WORKFLOW
=======================================================

Implement LeaseAccountingWorkflow:

Activities:
1. mark_running
2. load_leases_and_payments
3. build_payment_timeline
4. calculate_present_value
5. generate_liability_schedule
6. generate_rou_schedule
7. build_journal_preview
8. validate_lineage
9. finalize_run

Rules:
- workflow payload compact only:
  run_id, tenant_id, correlation_id, requested_by, config_hash
- heavy data read/written in DB-backed activities
- retries bounded
- validation errors non-retryable
- idempotent activity writes via natural keys and event idempotency

=======================================================
TESTS REQUIRED
=======================================================

Unit tests:
- lease registry append-only behavior
- payment schedule ordering and determinism
- PV calculation reproducibility
- liability schedule correctness
- ROU schedule correctness
- interest engine correctness

Edge cases:
- one lease, one payment
- same-currency lease/reporting

- month-end locked rate missing when required
- modification effective mid-schedule
- impairment present
- zero payment period
- lineage incomplete path must fail

========================================================
SECTION 1 — GLOBAL PLATFORM INVARIANTS
========================================================

Include ALL of the following invariants explicitly:

- All financial-impacting tables must be append-only.
- All financial-impacting tables must have RLS ENABLE + FORCE.
- All writes must go through AuditWriter.
- No direct session.add in financial paths.
- All financial outputs must be drillable.
- Every displayed financial value must be double-click navigable to base snapshot/source line.
- Every export must include cross-sheet links.
- Lineage completeness must be validated before terminal completion.
- Lifecycle must use immutable run header + append-only run events.
- Latest status must be derived, not stored mutably.
- All engines must remain modular.
- No bulk/monolithic files.
- Revenue, Lease, Prepaid, FAR must remain separate modules permanently.
- No cross-engine business logic leakage.
- All FX usage must go through selected-rate abstraction only.
- No raw FX provider table reads.
- Deterministic math only.
- No AI-generated accounting math.
- Temporal payloads must be compact (no heavy arrays).
- Idempotent request signatures required for mutation workflows.
- Supersession only via new rows; no in-place mutation.
- Correlation ID propagation mandatory.
- Multi-tenant isolation must be runtime enforced.
- Excel exports must be deterministic.
- Quantization policy must be centralized and consistent.
- Journal namespace must be engine-specific (REV-, LSE-, PPD-, FAR-).

CRITICAL MISSING ITEMS FOR $1B SCALABILITY:
1. Data Architecture Gaps
No columnar storage strategy - Append-only tables will explode in size; need columnar compression for financial data at scale

No data lifecycle policy - Rules for hot/warm/cold data, archival, and purging (especially for append-only tables)

No partition strategy - How tables are partitioned by tenant, date, and entity type for query performance at 1000+ tenants

No read replica architecture - Analytics queries killing write performance without read replicas

2. Performance & Caching Gaps
No query performance SLAs - Maximum response times for drill-down operations at scale

No materialized view strategy - Pre-computed aggregates for common financial rollups

No cache invalidation rules - When and how financial caches are invalidated across tenants

No batch processing architecture - How nightly reconciliations scale beyond single-server processing

3. Multi-Tenancy Depth Gaps
No tenant isolation tiers - Different isolation levels (dedicated DB, shared DB, schema-per-tenant) based on customer size

No tenant migration strategy - How to move tenants between isolation tiers without downtime

No noisy neighbor protection - Rate limiting, concurrency controls, and resource quotas per tenant

4. Compliance & Regional Gaps
No data residency rules - Where financial data lives (GDPR, local financial regulations)

No sovereignty controls - Geographic restrictions on data processing and AI model training

No audit log retention policies - Different retention periods by regulation type and jurisdiction

5. Financial Scale Gaps
No transaction volume tiers - Different processing paths for SMB vs enterprise transaction volumes

No bulk processing engine - Handling month-end close for 10,000+ entities simultaneously

No parallel execution framework - Running reconciliations across entities in parallel with dependency management

6. AI/ML at Scale Gaps
No model versioning strategy - How AI models are versioned and rolled back when they produce incorrect financial outputs

No training data isolation - Preventing cross-tenant data leakage in AI training

No inference cost controls - Monitoring and limiting AI costs as query volume scales

7. Operational Scalability Gaps
No feature flag system - Rolling out financial features gradually to subsets of tenants

No dark launch capability - Testing new financial calculations in production without affecting users

No canary deployment rules - How financial system upgrades are validated before full rollout

8. Business Continuity Gaps
No RTO/RPO by tenant tier - Recovery time objectives by customer value (enterprise vs SMB)

No financial reconciliation after disaster - Process to verify data integrity after recovery

No regional failover rules - Which regions take over during outages and how financial locks are handled

9. Cost Management Gaps
No storage cost attribution - Tracking append-only storage costs by tenant for profitability analysis

No compute cost allocation - Attributing processing costs to specific features and tenants

No infrastructure auto-scaling rules - When and how to scale resources based on financial calendar events (month-end, year-end)

10. Integration Scale Gaps
No webhook throttling - Rate limiting outbound webhooks to prevent overwhelming customer systems

No integration retry with backoff - Exponential backoff for failed external system calls

No bulk API limits - Restrictions on large data exports to prevent system overload

CRITICAL INVARIANT TO ADD:
Tenant Resource Quotas: Every tenant must have defined quotas for API calls, storage, concurrent jobs, and data exports to prevent single-tenant resource exhaustion affecting platform stability.

VALUATION READINESS CHECK:
At $1B valuation, you'll need:

SOC2 Type II + ISO 27001 certifications

Financial data immutability verified by third-party audit

Penetration testing reports for financial systems

Disaster recovery tests documented quarterly

99.95% uptime SLA with financial penalties

Without these items, you'll hit scalability walls at 100-200 tenants or $10-20M ARR, long before $1B valuation.

You kept control plane separate from finance engines.
That is correct and must remain so.

2. Correct hierarchy intent
You included:

user

organisation

group

entity

That is essential for enterprise structure.

3. Correct workflow direction
You included:

initiator

reviewer

approver

multiple users per role

process/module mapping

That is exactly what enterprise finance workflows need.

4. Correct quota thinking
Putting quotas into the control plane is the right move.
This should not live inside revenue/lease/consolidation services.

5. Correct enablement model
Package + module + feature flag is the right control stack.

Mandatory clarifications before implementation
A. Hierarchy model must be explicitly normalized
You need to decide this clearly:

Is organisation the tenant root?

Is group optional under organisation?

Are entities always children of organisation, or can they belong to groups only?

Can one entity belong to multiple groups?

Recommended answer
Use:

Tenant
  └─ Organisation
       ├─ Group (optional)
       └─ Entity
And define:

entity belongs to one organisation

entity may belong to zero or one group initially

do not allow many-to-many group membership yet unless absolutely required

Otherwise complexity explodes.

B. RBAC must separate role from permission from assignment
Do not blur these concepts.

You need distinct layers:

roles

permissions

role_permissions

user_role_assignments

module_overrides or equivalent

Because if you hardcode rights into role tables, future module growth becomes painful.

Audit result
Likely present conceptually, but this must be explicit in implementation.

C. Workflow mapping must support both role-based and named-user assignment
This is critical.

Some approvals are:

anyone in reviewer pool can act

Others are:

this exact CFO or controller must approve

So workflow design must support:

role-based stage assignment

named-user stage assignment

multiple users per stage

escalation / delegation

If the plan only says “multiple users per role,” that is not enough.

D. Quotas need hard enforcement points
The design must define exactly where quotas are enforced:

API ingress

Job submission

Worker execution

Export generation

Storage growth

AI usage

If quotas are only checked at API layer, users will still overload jobs through async paths.

Required
Every quota type needs:

metric source

enforcement point

breach behavior

E. Isolation tiers need a routing contract
You cannot just store “tier.”

You must define:

how DB/session routing changes by tenant tier

how storage routing changes

how background workers discover tenant routing

what migration state looks like during cutover

Otherwise “isolation tier” is just metadata, not architecture.

Recommended architecture decisions
These should be locked before implementation.

1. Core control-plane tables
At minimum, implementation should include:

tenants

organisations

groups

entities

users

user_organisation_assignments

user_entity_assignments

packages

tenant_package_assignments

module_registry

tenant_module_enablements

feature_flags

roles

permissions

role_permissions

user_role_assignments

workflow_templates

workflow_stages

workflow_role_assignments

workflow_user_assignments

quota_policies

tenant_quota_assignments

tenant_usage_counters

tenant_isolation_tiers

tenant_migration_events

That is the minimum serious control-plane surface.

2. Workflow role model
Each workflow stage should support:

stage_type

stage_sequence

approval_mode (single, any_of, all_of)

assigned_role_ids

assigned_user_ids

escalation_after_minutes

delegation_allowed

minimum_approvals_required

This will save you later.

3. Quota model
Each quota should include:

quota_type

hard_limit

soft_limit

current_usage

reset_window

enforcement_mode (reject, queue, throttle)

burst_limit (optional)

Risk assessment by topic
Low risk
control plane separation

feature flag inclusion

Medium risk
hierarchy over-complexity

RBAC over-simplification

workflow modeling ambiguity

High risk
quotas without multi-layer enforcement

isolation tiers without routing contract

migration strategy without transitional state model

Must clarify before implementation

🔍 CODEX AUDIT PROMPT — PHASE 1E CONTROL PLANE
You are to perform a strict architectural audit of:

docs/PHASE_1E_PLATFORM_CONTROL_PLANE.md

This is not a summary task.
This is not a rewrite task.
This is a structural audit.

Your objective:
Identify structural weaknesses, ambiguity, missing enforcement contracts, normalization issues, or scalability risks in the Phase 1E design.

========================================================
AUDIT SCOPE
========================================================

Audit the document across the following domains:

1. Hierarchy normalization
2. RBAC model separation
3. Workflow & approval engine robustness
4. Quota enforcement completeness
5. Isolation tier routing contract
6. Feature flag isolation safety
7. Control-plane interception correctness
8. RLS & governance enforcement consistency
9. Multi-tenant scaling risks
10. Migration & upgrade risk
11. Cross-module contamination risk

========================================================
AUDIT QUESTIONS TO ANSWER
========================================================

SECTION A — HIERARCHY

- Is the tenant → organisation → group → entity hierarchy unambiguous?
- Are many-to-many relationships properly controlled?
- Can users belong to multiple organisations/entities?
- Are manager/reviewer/approver mappings normalized or duplicated?
- Is soft-deactivation handled safely?

Flag any over-complication or under-specification.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION B — RBAC

- Are roles separated from permissions?
- Is permission evaluation dynamic or static?
- Are module-level overrides supported?
- Can role explosion occur?
- Is least-privilege enforceable?
- Is privilege escalation risk addressed?

Flag structural weakness.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION C — WORKFLOW ENGINE

- Does workflow design support:
    - Sequential approvals
    - Parallel approvals
    - Role-based assignment
    - Named-user assignment
    - Delegation
    - Escalation
- Are workflow templates versioned?
- Is workflow state append-only?
- Are race conditions possible?

Flag ambiguity or risk.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION D — QUOTAS

- Are enforcement points defined at:
    - API ingress
    - Job submission
    - Worker execution
    - Export layer
    - AI usage layer
    - Storage growth
- Are quota resets defined?
- Is burst handling defined?
- Is metering tenant-scoped?
- Can async paths bypass quota checks?

Flag any incomplete enforcement.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION E — ISOLATION TIERS

- Is tier routing operationally defined or only conceptual?
- Is DB/session routing specified?
- Is worker routing specified?
- Is migration state modeled?
- Is cutover deterministic?

Flag missing routing contract.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION F — FEATURE FLAGS

- Are feature flags tenant-scoped?
- Are flags versioned?
- Is dark launch safe?
- Is rollback deterministic?

Flag missing guardrails.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION G — CONTROL-PLANE INTERCEPTION

- Is interception mandatory before finance execution?
- Is there any path that bypasses control-plane validation?
- Are async workflows also intercepted?
- Is enforcement centralized?

Flag any bypass risk.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION H — RLS & GOVERNANCE

- Are all control-plane tables RLS ENABLE + FORCE?
- Are writes AuditWriter-only?
- Are append-only constraints defined where required?
- Are lifecycle events immutable?

Flag any inconsistency.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION I — SCALE RISK

- Does the model scale to 1,000 tenants?
- Does RBAC scale without role explosion?
- Does workflow scale under parallel approvals?
- Do quotas scale under heavy usage?
- Does isolation model scale?

Flag performance or structural bottlenecks.

--------------------------------------------------------

SECTION J — IMPLEMENTATION RISK

- Are there circular dependencies?
- Is there tight coupling to finance engines?
- Can module purity be accidentally violated?
- Is test coverage strategy defined?

Flag integration risk.

========================================================
OUTPUT FORMAT
========================================================

Return:

1. PASS / FAIL summary for each section (A–J)
2. Detailed findings (bullet points)

   - Ready for implementation

1) PASS / FAIL Summary (A–J)

Section	Domain	Result
A	Hierarchy normalization	FAIL
B	RBAC model separation	FAIL
C	Workflow & approval robustness	FAIL
D	Quota enforcement completeness	FAIL
E	Isolation tier routing contract	FAIL

G	Control-plane interception correctness	FAIL
H	RLS & governance consistency	FAIL

2) Detailed Findings (with severity and remediation)

Section A — Hierarchy

[HIGH] Role semantics are duplicated between hierarchy maps and RBAC (mapping_role in cp_user_organisation_map/cp_user_entity_map at L143/L162, plus RBAC roles at L269-L305), creating authorization drift risk. Remediation: separate membership from authorization; keep org/entity membership tables role-free and resolve permissions only through cp_user_roles with deterministic scope precedence.
[HIGH] Soft-deactivation is internally contradictory (status change on row at L79-L80 vs append-only state/event language at L178-L181). Remediation: define explicit append-only principal state event table and projection model; prohibit direct status mutation on base history rows.
[MEDIUM] Hierarchy integrity constraints are incomplete: no explicit cycle-prevention for org tree (parent_organisation_id, L90) and no explicit rule enforcing entity-group-organisation consistency. Remediation: add hierarchy acyclic constraint strategy and composite integrity constraints tying entity/group/org within tenant.
[MEDIUM] Temporal membership windows can overlap without exclusion constraints (effective_from/effective_to maps at L145-L169). Remediation: add non-overlap exclusion constraints per user-scope-role tuple.
Section B — RBAC

[HIGH] Least-privilege and segregation-of-duties are not explicit (for example, initiator approving own workflow not prohibited). Remediation: add SoD policies in permission evaluator and approval write guards.
[MEDIUM] Scope conflict resolution is unspecified across tenant/organisation/entity/workflow_template/module contexts (L301-L303). Remediation: define deterministic precedence matrix and deny-over-allow rule.
[MEDIUM] Role explosion controls are missing (tenant-defined roles + contextual grants can grow combinatorially). Remediation: add role template governance, max custom-role limits, and review workflow for new role creation.
[MEDIUM] Privilege escalation controls are incomplete: inheritance acyclic rule exists, but depth/override/fail-safe behavior is not specified (L274, L328-L333). Remediation: enforce max inheritance depth, explicit inheritance resolution order, and cycle/depth validation at write time.
Section C — Workflow & Approval Engine

[HIGH] Workflow template versioning is missing (UNIQUE (tenant_id, template_code) at L353, no version/effective fields). Remediation: introduce append-only template version table; bind instances to immutable template_version_id.
[HIGH] Stateful mutable columns (status in workflow and stage instances at L387/L397) conflict with append-only lifecycle expectations and can race under concurrency. Remediation: adopt event-sourced status derivation with immutable events and projection-only status fields.
[CRITICAL] Approval idempotency/race protections are absent in cp_workflow_approvals (L404-L414 has no uniqueness/idempotency key). Remediation: add idempotency key + unique constraints (for example per stage/actor/decision window) and optimistic concurrency checks.
[MEDIUM] Named-user assignment is under-specified; only role maps and delegations are modeled (L368-L377, L416-L426). Remediation: add explicit stage assignee table for named users and deterministic fallback logic.
[MEDIUM] Escalation target is mentioned in prose (L435-L438) but not represented in schema. Remediation: add escalation configuration fields/tables with role/user target, SLA, and escalation policy version.
Section D — Quotas

[HIGH] Enforcement points omit explicit export-layer, AI gateway, and storage growth controls in enforcement section (L480-L483), despite quota types including those dimensions (L461-L462). Remediation: define enforcement contracts for export service, AI ingress, and storage allocator.
[HIGH] cp_tenant_quota_usage lacks idempotency dimensions and uniqueness strategy (L471-L478), enabling retry double-counting. Remediation: add operation/request signature and atomic upsert/increment semantics with unique keys.
[MEDIUM] Quota reset semantics are not defined (fixed/sliding windows, reset jobs, carryover). Remediation: define per-quota window algorithm and reset lifecycle contract.
[MEDIUM] Async bypass risk remains for non-Temporal background paths; only “critical activity stage” re-check is specified (L578-L582). Remediation: require centralized quota guard in all worker executors and enforce via integration tests.
Section E — Isolation Tiers

[HIGH] routing_key is opaque and not operationally bound to DB/session/queue/worker routing (L502). Remediation: define typed routing contract (db_cluster, schema, worker_pool, region) with validation rules.
[HIGH] Worker routing by isolation tier is not explicitly defined. Remediation: add worker-pool mapping policy per tier and admission controls to prevent cross-tier execution leakage.
[MEDIUM] Migration state is coarse (active/migrating/rollback_pending, L503) and not step-materialized for deterministic resume. Remediation: add append-only migration run/events tables with step idempotency and retry state.
[MEDIUM] Cutover is described as atomic (L526-L529) but lock/consistency contract is not explicit. Remediation: define deterministic cutover transaction boundaries, lock scope, and replay checkpoint semantics.
Section F — Feature Flags

[HIGH] dark_launch safety is ambiguous (L540): side effects may run while outputs are hidden. Remediation: split flag effects into explicit compute_enabled, write_enabled, visibility_enabled controls.
[MEDIUM] flag_value JSONB schema is untyped and unversioned (L240-L251, L544-L549). Remediation: add flag schema version + JSON schema validation and rollout policy validation.
[HIGH] Overlapping effective windows and conflict resolution are not defined for flags. Remediation: enforce non-overlap constraints per tenant/module/flag_key and deterministic precedence rules.
Section G — Control-Plane Interception

[CRITICAL] Interception is defined as interface policy (ControlPlaneAuthorizer, L49) but no fail-closed enforcement contract is defined for direct internal execution paths. Remediation: enforce mandatory gate middleware/decorator at all command handlers with static checks that reject ungated routes.
[HIGH] Bypass prevention for async/non-API initiators is not fully formalized. Remediation: require signed authorization token/context issued by control-plane gate and verified by finance command executors.
[MEDIUM] defer outcome is defined (L54) but queue ownership, expiry, and replay semantics are not specified. Remediation: define deferred-request lifecycle schema and timeout/escalation policy.
Section H — RLS & Governance

[HIGH] “All control-plane tables MUST have tenant policy” (L587-L590) conflicts with global tables lacking tenant_id (cp_packages L195-L201, cp_permissions L280-L285). Remediation: explicitly classify global registry tables vs tenant-scoped tables and define distinct RLS policies.
[HIGH] Workflow events are referenced (cp_workflow_events, L446-L453) but schema contract is missing, weakening immutability guarantees. Remediation: define full event table schema with event_seq, idempotency_key, and uniqueness constraints.
[MEDIUM] AuditWriter-only rule is declared (L605-L607) but table-level write contract and exception handling are not specified. Remediation: define canonical write APIs and explicit prohibited direct-write patterns with test assertions.
Section I — Scale Risks

[HIGH] RBAC evaluation at runtime can become join-heavy at 1,000 tenants without caching/materialization strategy. Remediation: add permission snapshot/cache plan with invalidation on role grant/revoke events.
[HIGH] Quota usage write model can hotspot under high throughput without partitioning/aggregation. Remediation: add per-tenant partitioning, rolling aggregate buckets, and write coalescing.
[HIGH] Parallel approvals can race under high concurrency without idempotent decision semantics. Remediation: add deterministic decision state machine and concurrency control keys.
[MEDIUM] Isolation policy resolution appears centralized and may become control-plane choke point. Remediation: add cached routing snapshots with versioned invalidation and regional replicas.
Section J — Implementation / Integration Risks

[MEDIUM] engine_context enum hard-codes finance engine names (L219), creating schema-coupling to module evolution. Remediation: externalize engine/module registry with extensible codes and migration-safe onboarding contract.
[HIGH] Role duplication between hierarchy maps and RBAC introduces cross-module contamination and circular governance ownership. Remediation: enforce single authority for authorization semantics and keep hierarchy tables identity-only.
[MEDIUM] Test strategy exists (L647-L654) but missing explicit fail-closed interception tests, routing-key integrity tests, and concurrency race tests. Remediation: add mandatory suites for bypass denial, migration rollback determinism, and parallel approval race safety.
3) Overall Phase 1E Readiness Score

62 / 100
4) Recommendation

Needs clarification pass

What the audit is really saying
The design is conceptually correct
You have the right major parts:

hierarchy

RBAC

workflow approvals

quotas

isolation tiers

feature flags

interception layer

So the foundation is fine.

The problem is enforcement ambiguity
The biggest gaps are all about:

who is authoritative for permissions

how status is derived without mutable drift

how concurrency/idempotency is enforced

how quotas are actually enforced in async and non-API paths

how isolation tier routing becomes operational

how global vs tenant-scoped tables are governed

how to prevent bypass paths

Highest-priority issues from the audit
These are the items that matter most.

1. Role duplication between hierarchy and RBAC
This is a real problem.

Do not let organisation/entity membership tables carry authorization semantics.

Correct rule
hierarchy tables = identity and membership only

RBAC tables = authorization only

This must be fixed in the design before implementation.

2. Workflow state mutability conflict
If workflow/template/stage state becomes mutable, you will violate your own lifecycle invariant.

Correct rule
immutable header

append-only event log

latest state derived from events

No exceptions.

3. Approval race / idempotency missing
This is a critical issue.

Parallel approvals without idempotency and concurrency protection will break under real usage.

Correct rule
Each approval decision path must have:

idempotency key

unique constraint

optimistic concurrency rule

deterministic decision state machine

4. Control-plane interception is not yet fail-closed
This is another critical issue.

You cannot rely only on “everyone should call the gate.”

Correct rule
No finance command path may execute without a control-plane authorization token/context.

This must apply to:

API calls

async jobs

internal command handlers

retries

5. Quotas are not fully operationally enforced
Right now they sound like policy, not enforcement.

Correct rule
Every quota must define:

source metric

enforcement point

breach behavior

reset window

idempotent usage accounting

6. Isolation tier routing is too abstract
Storing a “routing_key” is not enough.

Correct rule
Routing contract must specify:

db_cluster

schema

worker_pool

region

migration state

7. Global vs tenant-scoped tables need explicit governance split
This is important.

Tables like:

packages

permissions

module registry

may be global, not tenant-scoped.

So you need two explicit table classes:

global registry tables

tenant-scoped control tables

Otherwise the RLS rule becomes inconsistent.

  - schema

  - region
  - migration_state

  - compute_enabled

  - API requests

  - global registry tables

Revised design decisions by section
Section 2 (L56): hierarchy/membership now explicitly identity-only; authorization removed from membership tables; identity status changed to append-only lifecycle projection.

Section 5 (L388): workflow state redesigned to immutable headers + append-only events; template versioning added; state derivation rules defined; approval idempotency and parallel concurrency behavior specified with deterministic state machine.
Section 6 (L585): quota model expanded to explicit per-type contracts (metric, enforcement point, breach behavior, reset window, idempotent accounting); async/internal bypass-proof rule added.
Section 7 (L648): abstract routing_key replaced by explicit routing contract (db_cluster, schema_name, worker_pool, region, migration_state, route_version); deterministic cutover/rollback semantics defined.
Section 8 (L707): dark-launch decomposed into explicit controls (compute_enabled, write_enabled, visibility_enabled); non-overlap + precedence rules defined.
Section 9 (L752): fail-closed interception contract added for API/background/internal/workflow paths; signed control-plane context token required before execution.
Section 10 (L808): global registry vs tenant-scoped table classification added; RLS expectations split accordingly; append-only/AuditWriter/correlation requirements aligned; scale hardening notes added.
Section 11 (L888): exit criteria updated for event-only workflow state, expanded quota enforcement points, fail-closed interception tests, and new flag model.
Explicit schema clarifications
Removed authorization fields from membership maps:
cp_user_organisation_map: removed mapping_role.
cp_user_entity_map: removed mapping_role.
Added RBAC clarification:
Section 4 is sole authorization source; membership is non-authorizing.
Workflow schema hardened:
Added cp_workflow_template_versions.
cp_workflow_instances and cp_workflow_stage_instances treated as immutable headers.
Added cp_workflow_instance_events and cp_workflow_stage_events with event_seq + idempotency_key uniqueness.
cp_workflow_approvals now includes idempotency_key and request_fingerprint unique constraints.
Added cp_workflow_stage_user_map for named-user assignment.
Quota schema hardened:
cp_tenant_quota_usage_events (append-only, idempotent keys).
cp_tenant_quota_windows (derived projection).
Isolation schema hardened:
cp_tenant_isolation_policy now includes db_cluster, schema_name, worker_pool, region, migration_state, route_version, effective dating.
Feature flag schema hardened:
rollout_mode reduced to off/on/canary.
Added compute_enabled, write_enabled, visibility_enabled.
Explicit enforcement contracts
Authorization/interception:
Central ControlPlaneAuthorizer plus mandatory signed context token; finance executors reject missing/invalid tokens.
Workflow state:
Current state derived only from highest event_seq; no mutable status writes.
Approval concurrency:
Idempotent approval writes + deterministic tally/recompute + single terminal-event semantics.
Quotas:
Central QuotaGuard.check_and_record(...) mandatory for API, async, and internal paths.
Isolation:
Route resolution must provide DB/session and worker routing attributes; missing attributes fail closed.
Flags:
Effective-window non-overlap, deterministic precedence, append-only rollback.
Governance:
Tenant-scoped tables require ENABLE + FORCE RLS; global registry tables use platform-admin controlled access model.
Revised readiness score estimate
Updated estimate: 91 / 100 (up from prior audit score) after removing major ambiguities and adding enforceable contracts.

Ready for implementation (design clarification pass complete; contracts are now explicit and implementation-oriented).

Absolutely. Below is the full Codex-ready Phase 1E implementation prompt, written to enforce the modular platform-control-plane structure we agreed on.

Phase 1E — Platform Control Plane Implementation Prompt
You are implementing Phase 1E — Platform Control Plane for FinanceOps / AI CFO Brain.

This is a PLATFORM CONTROL PLANE bounded context.
It is NOT a finance engine.
It must remain separate from Revenue, Lease, Prepaid, FAR, Consolidation, FX, MIS, and Reconciliation modules.

This phase must implement:
- tenant onboarding
- organisation/group/entity hierarchy
- package and module enablement
- RBAC
- workflow & approval engine
- tenant resource quotas
- isolation tier routing
- feature flags
- fail-closed control-plane interception

Do NOT implement finance business logic in this phase.

========================================================
MANDATORY ARCHITECTURAL RULES
========================================================

1. Control plane must be a separate bounded context.
2. Membership tables are identity-only, never authorization-bearing.
3. RBAC is the sole source of authorization truth.
4. Workflow state must use immutable headers + append-only events.
5. Approval decisions must be idempotent and concurrency-safe.
6. Quotas must be enforced at:
   - API ingress
   - job submission
   - worker execution
   - export generation
   - AI usage
   - storage growth
7. Isolation routing must be explicit and operational, not conceptual.
8. Feature flags must support:
   - compute_enabled
   - write_enabled
   - visibility_enabled
   - rollout_mode = off / on / canary
9. Finance execution must be fail-closed unless valid control-plane context token is present.
10. All new control-plane code must be modular. No monolithic files.
11. All writes must use AuditWriter where applicable.
12. Tenant-scoped control-plane tables must use RLS ENABLE + FORCE.
13. Global registry tables must be explicitly separated from tenant-scoped tables.
14. Correlation ID propagation is mandatory.
15. No direct session.add in control-plane write paths.
16. All code must be fully typed.

========================================================
TARGET DIRECTORY STRUCTURE
========================================================

Implement under a dedicated platform namespace.

Create/update only in modular structure like:

========================================================
IMPLEMENTATION SCOPE
========================================================

SECTION A — CORE HIERARCHY

Implement tenant-scoped identity hierarchy:

1. tenants
2. organisations
3. groups
4. entities
5. user_organisation_assignments
6. user_entity_assignments

Rules:
- membership only, not authorization
- no mapping_role in membership tables
- effective dating where relevant
- non-overlap protection where applicable
- soft-deactivation via append-only lifecycle/event-compatible pattern, not mutable status shortcuts
- entity belongs to one organisation
- group is optional
- keep group membership simple and deterministic

SECTION B — PACKAGE & MODULE ENABLEMENT

Implement:
- package registry
- tenant package assignment
- module registry
- tenant module enablement

Rules:
- global registry tables explicitly separated from tenant-scoped tables
- finance modules cannot execute if module disabled
- package upgrade/downgrade support
- module enablement checked by control-plane authorizer
- keep module registry extensible, not hardcoded to current engines only

SECTION C — RBAC

Implement distinct structures for:
- roles
- permissions
- role_permissions
- user_role_assignments

Rules:
- RBAC is sole source of authorization truth
- deterministic scope precedence must be implemented
- deny-over-allow rule must be explicit
- least privilege support
- segregation of duties support
- no role semantics in hierarchy tables
- avoid role explosion through clean normalization
- support platform scope, tenant scope, organisation scope, entity scope, module scope, workflow template scope as defined in design

SECTION D — WORKFLOWS & APPROVALS

Implement:
- workflow_templates
- workflow_template_versions
- workflow_instances
- workflow_stage_instances
- workflow_instance_events
- workflow_stage_events
- workflow_approvals
- workflow_stage_user_map

Rules:
- immutable headers + append-only events only
- latest status derived from highest event sequence
- template versioning mandatory
- named-user assignment supported
- role-based assignment supported
- approval idempotency mandatory
- request_fingerprint and idempotency_key required where designed
- parallel approvals must be concurrency-safe
- escalation hooks supported structurally
- delegation supported structurally
- no mutable state shortcuts

SECTION E — QUOTAS

Implement:
- quota policies
- tenant quota assignments
- tenant quota usage events
- tenant quota windows / projection table

Quota types must include:
- API calls
- concurrent jobs
- storage
- exports
- AI inference
- workflow concurrency

Rules:
- QuotaGuard.check_and_record(...) must be central enforcement mechanism
- enforce at API, async, internal command paths
- usage accounting must be idempotent
- breach behavior must support reject / queue / throttle
- reset windows must be explicit
- async paths must not bypass quota checks

SECTION F — ISOLATION TIERS

Implement explicit isolation routing contract with fields such as:
- db_cluster
- schema_name
- worker_pool
- region
- migration_state
- route_version
- effective dating

Implement:
- isolation policy table
- tenant migration events
- migration workflow scaffolding

Rules:
- routing must be operationally resolvable
- worker routing must be isolation-aware
- migration state must be append-only/event-compatible where relevant
- missing routing attributes fail closed

SECTION G — FEATURE FLAGS

Implement:
- tenant-scoped feature flags
- rollout_mode = off / on / canary
- compute_enabled
- write_enabled
- visibility_enabled

Rules:
- overlapping effective windows must be prevented or deterministically resolved
- precedence rules explicit
- rollback deterministic
- dark launch must not accidentally write when write_enabled = false

SECTION H — FAIL-CLOSED CONTROL-PLANE INTERCEPTION

Implement:
- ControlPlaneAuthorizer
- signed control-plane context token
- enforcement interceptors/decorators/middleware hooks as appropriate

Rules:
- no finance execution path may proceed without validated control-plane context
- applies to:
  - API requests
  - background jobs
  - internal command handlers
  - workflow-triggered execution
- missing or invalid token fails closed
- module enablement, RBAC, workflow eligibility, quota eligibility, and routing must be evaluated before finance execution

========================================================
DATA GOVERNANCE RULES
========================================================

1. Tenant-scoped control-plane tables:
- RLS ENABLE + FORCE
- tenant policy
- AuditWriter-governed writes where applicable

2. Global registry tables:
- explicit platform-admin controlled access model
- do not incorrectly force tenant RLS where tenant_id does not exist

3. Append-only:
- apply where events, policies, or materially governed records require immutability
- use event tables for lifecycle state
- avoid mutable status shortcuts

========================================================
TEMPORAL SCOPE
========================================================

Implement only control-plane workflows relevant to this phase:

1. TenantOnboardingWorkflow
2. TenantMigrationWorkflow

Rules:
- compact workflow payload only
- heavy data loaded from DB in activities
- idempotent event writes
- bounded retries
- fail-closed on missing control-plane invariants

========================================================
API / ENFORCEMENT FLOW
========================================================

Implement the control-plane path so the intended execution model is:

API Request
→ tenant validation
→ module enablement check
→ RBAC check
→ workflow eligibility check
→ quota check
→ isolation routing resolution
→ signed control-plane context token issuance/verification
→ finance engine execution

This flow must be enforceable, not just documented.

========================================================
TEST REQUIREMENTS
========================================================

Add tests for at least:

1. hierarchy membership without authorization leakage
2. RBAC deny-over-allow precedence
3. module disabled path blocks finance execution
4. named-user and role-based workflow assignment both work
5. approval idempotency
6. parallel approval race safety
7. quota breach at API layer
8. quota breach at async/internal path
9. feature flag precedence
10. compute_enabled/write_enabled/visibility_enabled behavior
11. isolation routing resolution
12. missing routing data fails closed
13. missing control-plane token rejected
14. invalid token rejected
15. tenant onboarding workflow correctness
16. tenant migration workflow deterministic state handling

========================================================
ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA
========================================================

Phase 1E is complete only if:

1. tenant/org/group/entity hierarchy exists and is normalized
2. RBAC is sole authorization source
3. workflow templates and approvals are versioned, append-only, and concurrency-safe
4. quotas are enforced across API + async + internal paths

6. feature flags support off/on/canary + compute/write/visibility controls
7. finance execution paths fail closed without valid control-plane authorization
8. deterministic full pipeline passes
9. modularity is preserved; no god files created

Good progress. This is a real control-plane implementation, not a sketch.

Verdict
Phase 1E is functionally strong but not freeze-ready yet.

Reason: three items still block a clean freeze:

no full deterministic end-to-end run

migration 0008 uses model metadata instead of frozen static DDL

fail-closed interception is not yet attached across all finance entrypoints

Those are not cosmetic. They are core platform guarantees.

What is solid
You got the important architecture right:

separate bounded context under platform/

identity-only membership tables

RBAC as sole authorization source

append-only workflow events

idempotent approvals

centralized quota guard

explicit isolation routing contract

feature flags with compute/write/visibility separation

signed control-plane context token

modular file sizes

That is the right shape.

What still needs to be closed
1. Full deterministic pipeline must pass
“DB unavailable” means the implementation is not yet operationally proven in the same way earlier phases were.

Before freeze, run the normal deterministic script and show:

total collected

passed

skipped

failed

runtime

Without that, we are trusting structure, not validating system behavior.

2. Migration 0008 must be static
This is important.

If 0008_phase1e_platform_control_plane.py creates tables from model metadata at runtime, that is risky for long-term migration immutability and replay safety.

Fix:

replace runtime metadata-driven creation with explicit frozen DDL in the migration

ensure replay is stable even if models evolve later

This is a must-fix before freeze.

3. Fail-closed interception must be universal
Right now you called out that token interception is implemented and testable, but not yet broadly attached to every finance API/worker entrypoint.

That means the platform has the mechanism, but not yet universal enforcement.

Before freeze, you need:

all finance API mutation paths gated

all workflow-triggered finance execution paths gated

all async/internal execution paths gated

tests proving ungated execution is rejected

Until then, the invariant is only partially realized.

Recommended next move
Do a Phase 1E closure pass only for these three items.

anything wrong as 1200+ lines of code is removed or it actually good

It is likely good, not automatically bad.

Removing 1200+ lines can be a very positive sign when the deleted code was:

runtime-generated migration logic

duplicated metadata-driven DDL

repeated boilerplate

dead or indirect code paths

unstable workaround code

And in your case, that is exactly what the closure report suggests happened.

Why the large deletion is probably healthy
The biggest clue is this line:

0008 rewritten to frozen explicit DDL statements (no runtime model metadata table creation)

That kind of refactor often removes a lot of code because metadata-driven migrations usually carry:

dynamic table creation helpers

model imports

generated reflection logic

large helper blocks

indirect creation paths

Replacing that with explicit migration operations is usually:

shorter

safer

more replayable

more audit-friendly

So a large net deletion there is often an improvement, not a problem.

The strongest evidence it is okay
You also have:

371 collected

366 passed

5 skipped

0 failed

That matters more than the raw line delta.

If 1200 lines were removed and:

migration replay still works

finance token enforcement works

approval race tests still pass

full deterministic pipeline is green

then the deletion is almost certainly removing complexity, not removing required behavior.

What I would still check
There are only three things I would inspect before feeling fully comfortable:

1. Where exactly was the deletion?
If most of the deletion is in:

0008_phase1e_platform_control_plane.py

temporary/generated helper files

old dynamic DDL scaffolding

then good.

If the deletion came from:

approval service logic

token enforcement logic

quota enforcement logic

then inspect more closely.

2. Why do these files exist?
I noticed in the review list:

backend/tmp_cp_ddl.sql

backend/tmp_cp_ddl_py.txt

Those look like temporary artifacts.

That is the only immediate yellow flag I see.

They should generally not remain in the repo unless you intentionally want them for audit/reference.
If they are just helper files created during migration rewriting, they should probably be removed before final freeze.

3. Did test coverage actually touch the changed areas?
From your report, yes:

finance route token enforcement

approval race safety

control plane authorizer

full deterministic suite

So the changed areas were not completely untested.

The 1200+ line reduction is probably a good cleanup, not a problem.

the suite is green

That combination usually means:

less code, better guarantees

Readiness assessment for Prepaid implementation
Status: Partially ready (governance foundation is in place; Prepaid core is not started).
Prepaid is currently scaffold-only: service_facade.py, prepaid_workflows.py, prepaid_activities.py.
The platform already supports deterministic run/event lifecycle, lineage contracts, RLS session context, append-only triggers, AuditWriter write path, selected-rate FX service, and control-plane token infrastructure.
Blocking clarifications remain before implementation is safe (custom pattern semantics, idempotency keys for regenerated schedules, module-scoped token enforcement, and source artifact contract for prepaid lineage).
Reusable platform components
Run/event lifecycle + idempotency + derived status: run_lifecycle.py, run_events_base.py, run_base_models.py, run_signature.py.
Lineage metadata + chain validation: lineage_contract.py.
Drill response base shape: accounting_common.py.
Deterministic quantization + journal namespace + export links: quantization_policy.py, journal_namespace.py, export_links.py.
Central audited write path: audit_writer.py.
Selected-rate FX surface (no raw provider dependency required in Prepaid): fx_rate_service.py.
RLS runtime session context for API and workers: deps.py, session.py.
Append-only DB trigger helpers and established pattern: append_only.py, revenue/lease migrations 0006_phase1d2_revenue_core.py, 0007_phase1d3_lease_core.py.
Control-plane enforcement stack exists: control_plane_authorizer.py, interceptors.py, context_token.py.
Required module boundaries
Prepaid must own only: prepaid registry, amortization pattern resolution, schedule generation, prepaid adjustments/remeasurement, prepaid journal preview, prepaid lineage validation, prepaid drilldown service, prepaid workflow facade.
Prepaid must reuse (not reimplement): accounting_common lifecycle/quantization/namespace/lineage utilities; FX selected-rate service; AuditWriter; control-plane token checks.
Prepaid must not include: revenue allocation logic, lease PV/interest logic, FAR depreciation logic, consolidation IC/elimination logic, raw FX provider fetching, platform control-plane authorizer internals.
Coupling risk to prevent: copying revenue/lease service_facade logic into one large prepaid file. Keep module split from day one.
Proposed prepaid data model
prepaid_runs
Controls: FinancialBase, RLS ENABLE+FORCE, append-only trigger, AuditWriter-only writes.
Key/idempotency: unique (tenant_id, request_signature).
Fields: initiated_by, configuration_json, workflow_id, correlation_id.
Lineage hooks: not required as source lineage root for run header.
prepaid_run_events
Controls: FinancialBase, RLS, append-only, AuditWriter-only.
Key/idempotency: unique (run_id, event_seq) and (run_id, event_type, idempotency_key).
Fields: metadata_json, correlation_id.
prepaids
Controls: FinancialBase, RLS, append-only, AuditWriter-only.
Required lineage hooks: parent_reference_id, source_reference_id, source_expense_reference, correlation_id.
Supersession: supersedes_id required for correction rows.
Natural key recommendation: (tenant_id, prepaid_code, created_at) with deterministic request-level duplicate prevention.
prepaid_amortization_schedule
Controls: FinancialBase, RLS, append-only, AuditWriter-only.
Lineage hooks: parent_reference_id (prepaid), source_reference_id (source snapshot/artifact line), correlation_id.
Natural key recommendation: unique (run_id, prepaid_id, amortization_date, schedule_version_token) to make retries safe.
Supersession: either supersedes_id or explicit schedule_generation_id linkage; one must be fixed up front.
prepaid_journal_entries
Controls: FinancialBase, RLS, append-only, AuditWriter-only.
Lineage hooks: parent_reference_id (schedule line), source_reference_id (source artifact), correlation_id.
Journal namespace: PPD-... via accounting_common namespace helper.
prepaid_adjustments
Controls: FinancialBase, RLS, append-only, AuditWriter-only.
Lineage hooks: parent_reference_id (prior schedule/run), source_reference_id (source adjustment artifact), correlation_id.
Supersession: supersedes_id required to chain adjustment versions.
Natural key/idempotency: unique (run_id, prepaid_id, effective_date, adjustment_type, idempotency_key).
Key risks and ambiguities
Custom amortization pattern ambiguity: must define contract (percent-per-period vs amount-per-period vs weighting factors) and validation invariants.
Request signature collision risk for ordered custom schedules: run_signature canonicalizer sorts lists; if order is semantically meaningful, include explicit sequence fields before signature generation.
Rounding drift risk: must lock use of quantization policy at each stage (allocation, schedule row, cumulative totals, journal generation).
Mid-period adjustment policy ambiguity: define prospective-only vs catch-up behavior and how superseded schedule lines are linked.
FX policy ambiguity: explicit rule needed for when month-end locked is mandatory vs when daily selected rate is allowed.
Control-plane module-token scope risk: finance router currently uses module-agnostic token validation in router.py; Prepaid should enforce module-specific token claim.
Workflow interception ambiguity: background Temporal activities use tenant session context, but explicit control-plane token verification in workflow paths is not yet standardized for engines.
Required drillability design
Drill path must be:
amortized_expense -> prepaid_amortization_schedule -> prepaids -> source snapshot/artifact.
Mandatory prepaid endpoints:
POST /api/v1/prepaid/run
GET /api/v1/prepaid/run/{run_id}
GET /api/v1/prepaid/results/{run_id}
GET /api/v1/prepaid/run/{run_id}/prepaids/{prepaid_id}
GET /api/v1/prepaid/run/{run_id}/schedule-lines/{schedule_id}
GET /api/v1/prepaid/run/{run_id}/journal-entries/{journal_id}
Response contract: inherit DrillResponseBase shape with parent_reference_id, source_reference_id, correlation_id, deterministic child_ids.
Lineage completeness gate before terminal complete:
each schedule line resolves to prepaid + source artifact/snapshot line;
each journal entry resolves to schedule line;
failed gate appends failed run event with LINEAGE_INCOMPLETE.
Required control-plane integration points
For prepaid API execution, enforce:
module enablement check,
RBAC evaluation,
workflow eligibility (if applicable),
quota check,
isolation route resolution,
valid control-plane context token.
Prepaid must be added under finance router dependency pattern and should use module-specific token checks.
For async/internal paths:
propagate correlation_id;
use tenant-scoped session (tenant_session) for RLS;
require validated execution context for internal command triggers where applicable.
Quota touchpoints to wire for Prepaid:
run submission (api_requests/job_submissions),
workflow fanout (worker_active_jobs),
export endpoints (export_bytes) if added in scope.
Recommended implementation sequence
Lock prepaid scope and out-of-scope policy.
Finalize prepaid data contract (including custom pattern schema and adjustment semantics).
Add prepaid DB model + migration with explicit RLS policies and append-only triggers.
Add prepaid Pydantic schemas and validation rules.
Implement prepaid modular services (registry, pattern resolver, schedule generator, journal preview, remeasurement, lineage validation, drilldown).
Implement prepaid service facade using accounting_common lifecycle + AuditWriter only.
Implement prepaid Temporal workflow/activities with compact payload and idempotent DB writes.
Implement prepaid API routes and router registration with fail-closed control-plane token checks.
Add unit + integration tests (append-only, RLS runtime, idempotency, FX selected-rate path, drillability, lineage gate, control-plane rejection).
Run deterministic full suite and module-purity/file-size sanity check.
Recommendation
Needs clarification first.
Platform foundations are strong enough to start immediately after resolving the noted design ambiguities (especially custom pattern contract, supersession/idempotency keys, and module-scoped control-plane enforcement rules).
